###begin article-title 0
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 19 21 19 21 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 80 82 80 82 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 86 87 86 87 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 102 105 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">Rat</span>
[11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714 as New PET Tracers for TSPO: A Comparison with [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in a Rat Model of Herpes Encephalitis
###end article-title 0
###begin title 1
Background
###end title 1
###begin p 2
###xml 121 123 121 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 127 128 127 128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 235 237 235 237 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 241 242 241 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 375 377 375 377 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 393 395 393 395 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 456 459 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
Activation of microglia cells plays an important role in neurological diseases. Positron emission tomography (PET) with [11C]-(R)-PK11195 has already been used to visualize activated microglia cells in neurological diseases. However, [11C]-(R)-PK11195 may not possess the required sensitivity to visualize mild neuroinflammation. In this study, we evaluated the PET tracers [11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714 as agents for imaging of activated microglia in a rat model of herpes encephalitis.
###end p 2
###begin title 3
Materials and Methods
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 131 133 131 133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 137 138 137 138 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 150 152 150 152 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 169 171 169 171 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 0 4 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">Rats</span>
###xml 39 44 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
Rats were intranasally inoculated with HSV-1. On day 6 or 7 after inoculation, small animal PET studies were performed to compare [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714.
###end p 4
###begin title 5
Results
###end title 5
###begin p 6
###xml 11 13 11 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 81 82 81 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 98 100 98 100 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 170 172 170 172 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 207 209 207 209 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 213 214 213 214 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 255 257 255 257 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 299 301 299 301 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 305 306 305 306 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
Uptake of [11C]-DPA-713 in infected brain areas was comparable to that of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, but [11C]-DPA-713 showed lower non-specific binding. Non-specific uptake of [18F]-DPA-714 was lower than that of [11C]-(R)-PK11195. In the infected brain, total [18F]-DPA-714 uptake was lower than that of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, with comparable specific uptake.
###end p 6
###begin title 7
Conclusions
###end title 7
###begin p 8
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 75 77 75 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 81 82 81 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 121 123 121 123 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
[11C]-DPA-713 may be more suitable for visualizing mild inflammation than [11C]-(R)-PK11195. In addition, the fact that [18F]-DPA-714 is an agonist PET tracer opens new possibilities to evaluate different aspects of neuroinflammation. Therefore, both tracers warrant further investigation in animal models and in a clinical setting.
###end p 8
###begin title 9
Key words
###end title 9
###begin title 10
Introduction
###end title 10
###begin p 11
###xml 161 162 161 162 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">1</xref>
###xml 603 604 603 604 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
Neurological disorders are a significant burden to society worldwide, especially in countries where a growing proportion of the population is over 65 years old [1]. Despite the large difference between neurological disorders, neuroinflammation is involved in both acute pathology, such as stroke and herpes encephalitis, and chronic neurodegenerative diseases, such as Parkinson's and Alzheimer's disease. Although neuroinflammation was found to be involved in neurological disorders, it is still not known when the inflammatory response is beneficial, detrimental, or incidental. Nakajima and Kohsaka [2] proposed that neuroinflammation in acute injuries is beneficial, whereas it will lead to neuronal cell death in chronic diseases. When the exact role of neuroinflammation in different neurological disorders is unraveled, this will inevitably lead to early diagnosis, possible therapeutic intervention, and improved treatment.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 300 301 300 301 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR3">3</xref>
###xml 303 304 303 304 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR4">4</xref>
One of the key players in neuroinflammation is the microglia cell, which provides the first line of defense against brain tissue injuries. In the healthy central nervous system, microglia cells continuously survey their microenvironment by rapid extension and extraction of their ramified processes [3, 4]. In response to a wide variety of central nervous system insults, microglia cells become activated and change from their ramified state into amoeboid morphology. The activation of microglia cells is accompanied by an increased expression of the translocator protein (TSPO), an 18 kDa component of a heteromeric complex. The expression of the TSPO is low in the healthy brain, but is highly upregulated in neuroinflammation.
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 303 305 303 305 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 309 310 309 310 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 322 323 322 323 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 325 326 325 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</italic>
###xml 334 335 334 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</italic>
###xml 415 417 415 417 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 421 422 421 422 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 468 470 468 470 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 474 475 474 475 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 568 569 568 569 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR5">5</xref>
###xml 570 571 570 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR8">8</xref>
###xml 594 595 594 595 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR9">9</xref>
###xml 596 598 596 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">12</xref>
###xml 622 624 622 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR13">13</xref>
###xml 648 650 648 650 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR14">14</xref>
###xml 652 654 652 654 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">15</xref>
###xml 682 684 682 684 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR16">16</xref>
###xml 685 687 685 687 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">18</xref>
###xml 841 843 841 843 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 847 848 847 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
Positron emission tomography (PET) is a non-invasive imaging technique that can be used to study the role of neuroinflammation in neurological disorders, using the TSPO as a biomarker. PET has already been used in numerous clinical studies to visualize activated microglia cells using the isoquinoline [11C]-(R)-PK11195 ((R)-N-methyl-N-(1-methylpropyl)-1-(2-chlorophenyl)isoquinoline-3-carboxamide) as the tracer. [11C]-(R)-PK11195 is a ligand for the TSPO. Although [11C]-(R)-PK11195 has already been used to image activated microglia cells in, among others, stroke [5-8], multiple sclerosis [9-12], herpes encephalitis [13], Parkinson's disease [14, 15], and Alzheimer's disease [16-18], it is not an ideal tracer, since it shows low brain uptake and high non-specific binding. Pharmacokinetic modeling of the PET data is complicated and [11C]-(R)-PK11195 may not possess the sensitivity to visualize mild neuroinflammation, which makes it unsuitable for use in early diagnosis and detection of subtle effects of therapeutic intervention.
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 311 319 311 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vitro</italic>
###xml 392 394 392 394 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">19</xref>
###xml 395 397 395 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR21">21</xref>
###xml 469 476 469 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
###xml 498 500 498 500 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 526 528 526 528 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 672 674 672 674 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 732 734 732 734 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 738 739 738 739 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 857 859 857 859 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 1088 1090 1088 1090 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">19</xref>
###xml 1092 1094 1092 1094 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">20</xref>
###xml 490 496 <span type="species:ncbi:9557">baboon</span>
###xml 754 757 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 1054 1057 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
Therefore, a more sensitive and specific PET tracer for TSPO imaging would be of great interest. Pyrazolopyrimidines display high affinity for the TSPO and two compounds from this class have already been radiolabeled for use in PET. The pyrazolopyrimidines DPA-713 and DPA-714 have higher affinity for the TSPO in vitro (Ki = 4.7 nM and Ki = 7.0 nM, respectively) than PK11195 (Ki = 9.3 nM) [19-21]. The TSPO antagonist DPA-713 was labeled with carbon-11 and evaluated in vivo in a healthy baboon [22]. It was concluded that [11C]-DPA-713 is a specific ligand for the TSPO and that it may be useful for studying changes in the density of TSPO binding sites. In addition, [11C]-DPA-713 exhibited a higher signal-to-noise ratio than [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in a rat model of neurodegeneration, which makes it more suitable for quantification of TSPO binding sites [23]. The TSPO agonist, DPA-714, was labeled with fluorine-18 and demonstrated good uptake in the primate brain and an eightfold higher uptake in the lesioned striatum of a quinolinic acid-lesioned rat model of activated microglia [19, 20]. This higher uptake was shown to be selective TSPO binding.
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 6 8 6 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 24 26 24 26 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 131 133 131 133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">19</xref>
###xml 135 137 135 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">20</xref>
###xml 139 141 139 141 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 534 536 534 536 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 552 554 552 554 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 641 643 641 643 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 647 648 647 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 125 129 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 339 342 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 585 588 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
Both [11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714 have demonstrated better imaging properties than [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in striatum-lesioned rats [19, 20, 23]. However, striatum lesion by injection of a toxic compound requires invasive manipulations to generate an inflammatory response. The aim of this study was to validate these tracers in a different rat model that does not require invasive manipulation and unnatural toxic compounds to evoke neuroinflammation, which may better mimic microglia activation in neurological disorders. Therefore, [11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714 were evaluated in a rat model of herpes encephalitis (HSE) and compared to [11C]-(R)-PK11195.
###end p 15
###begin title 16
Materials and Methods
###end title 16
###begin title 17
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 7 8 7 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
[11C]-(R)-PK11195
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 7 8 7 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 43 45 43 45 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR24">24</xref>
###xml 90 91 90 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 93 94 93 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N</italic>
###xml 459 460 450 451 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 462 463 453 454 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 951 952 939 940 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1068 1069 1056 1057 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1071 1072 1059 1060 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
[11C]-(R)-PK11195 was labeled by trapping [11C]-methyl iodide [24] in a solution of 1 mg (R)-N-desmethyl PK11195 and 10 mg potassium hydroxide in 300 mul dimethylsulfoxide. The reaction mixture was allowed to react for 1 min at 40degreesC, neutralized with 1 M HCl, and passed through a 45-mum Millex HV filter. The filtrate was purified by high-performance liquid chromatography (HPLC) using a muBondapak C18 column (7.8 x 300 mm) with acetonitrile/25 mM NaH2PO4 (pH 3.5) (55/45) as the eluent (flow 5 ml/min). To remove the organic solvents from the product, the collected HPLC fraction (retention time 7 min) was diluted with 100 ml of water and passed through an Oasis HLB 30 mg (1 cc) cartridge. The cartridge was washed twice with 10 ml of water and subsequently eluted with 0.7 ml of ethanol and 5 ml of water. The product was sterilized by filtration over a 22 mum Millex LG filter. The product was obtained in 33 +/- 15% radiochemical yield (n = 11). Quality control was performed by HPLC, using a Novapak C18 column (150 x 3.9 mm) with acetonitrile/25 mM NaH2PO4 (pH 3.5; 60/40) as the eluent at a flow of 1 ml/min. The radiochemical purity was always >95% and the specific activity was 51 +/- 18 MBq/nmol.
###end p 18
###begin title 19
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
[11C]-DPA-713 (Compound 2)
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 23 26 23 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N,N</italic>
###xml 44 46 44 46 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 88 93 88 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#945;</italic>
###xml 133 135 129 131 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 148 150 144 146 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 203 206 199 202 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N,N</italic>
###xml 263 268 259 260 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#945;</italic>
###xml 308 310 300 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 367 368 358 359 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 579 580 563 564 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 582 583 566 567 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 1043 1044 1024 1025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1160 1161 1141 1142 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1163 1164 1144 1145 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 1239 1241 1220 1222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 1317 1324 1296 1303 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;1.</label>
###xml 1324 1638 1303 1617 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="21">Synthesis of DPA-713 from the labeling precursor compound 1 and DPA-714 from the labeling precursor compound 3. The labeling precursor compound 3 and the reference material for DPA-714 were synthesized from compound 1 using ethyleneglycol ditosylate and 2-fluoroethyltosylate as the alkylating agent, respectively.</p>
###xml 1324 1638 1303 1617 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><p textid="21">Synthesis of DPA-713 from the labeling precursor compound 1 and DPA-714 from the labeling precursor compound 3. The labeling precursor compound 3 and the reference material for DPA-714 were synthesized from compound 1 using ethyleneglycol ditosylate and 2-fluoroethyltosylate as the alkylating agent, respectively.</p></caption>
###xml 1638 1638 1617 1617 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" position="anchor" xlink:href="11307_2009_211_Fig1_HTML" id="MO1"/>
###xml 1317 1638 1296 1617 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Fig1"><label>Fig.&#160;1.</label><caption><p textid="21">Synthesis of DPA-713 from the labeling precursor compound 1 and DPA-714 from the labeling precursor compound 3. The labeling precursor compound 3 and the reference material for DPA-714 were synthesized from compound 1 using ethyleneglycol ditosylate and 2-fluoroethyltosylate as the alkylating agent, respectively.</p></caption><graphic position="anchor" xlink:href="11307_2009_211_Fig1_HTML" id="MO1"/></fig>
For the preparation of N,N-diethyl-2-(2-(4-[11C]methoxyphenyl)-5,7-dimethylpyrazolo(1,5-alpha)pyrimidin-3-yl)acetamide (compound 2, [11C]DPA-713), [11C]-methyl triflate was trapped in a solution of 1 mg N,N-diethyl-2-(2-(4-hydroxyphenyl)-5,7-dimethylpyrazolo(1,5-alpha)pyrimidin-3-yl)acetamide (compound 1) [22] and 2.5 mul 0.5 M NaOH in 0.5 ml of acetonitrile (Fig. 1). After 5 min at 100degreesC, the reaction mixture was diluted with 0.5 ml of acetonitrile and 1 ml of water and purified by HPLC using a SymmetryPrep C18 column (7 mum, 7.8 x 300 mm) and acetonitrile/0.1 M NaH2PO4 (1/1) as the eluent (flow 5 ml/min). The radioactive product with a retention time of 7-8 min was collected. The product was diluted with 100 ml of water and passed through an Oasis HLB 30 mg (1 cc) cartridge. The cartridge was washed twice with 10 ml of water and subsequently eluted with 0.7 ml of ethanol and 5 ml of water. The product was sterilized by filtration over a 22-mum Millex LG filter. The product is obtained in 48 +/- 15% radiochemical yield (n = 10). Quality control was performed by HPLC, using a Novapak C18 column (150 x 3.9 mm) with acetonitrile/25 mM NaH2PO4 (40/60) as the eluent at a flow of 1 ml/min. The radiochemical purity of [11C]DPA-713 was always >99% and the specific activity was 41 +/- 12 MBq/nmol. Fig. 1.Synthesis of DPA-713 from the labeling precursor compound 1 and DPA-714 from the labeling precursor compound 3. The labeling precursor compound 3 and the reference material for DPA-714 were synthesized from compound 1 using ethyleneglycol ditosylate and 2-fluoroethyltosylate as the alkylating agent, respectively.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
Synthesis of DPA-713 from the labeling precursor compound 1 and DPA-714 from the labeling precursor compound 3. The labeling precursor compound 3 and the reference material for DPA-714 were synthesized from compound 1 using ethyleneglycol ditosylate and 2-fluoroethyltosylate as the alkylating agent, respectively.
###end p 21
###begin title 22
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N,N</italic>
###xml 74 79 74 75 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#945;</italic>
N,N-diethyl-2-(2-(4-[2-tosyloxy-1-ethoxy]phenyl)-5,7-dimethylpyrazolo(1,5-alpha)pyrimidin-3-yl)acetamide (Compound 3)
###end title 22
###begin p 23
###xml 116 119 116 119 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N,N</italic>
###xml 176 181 176 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#945;</italic>
###xml 221 223 217 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 241 242 237 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 922 923 918 919 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 934 935 930 931 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 947 952 943 944 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#948;</italic>
###xml 966 967 958 959 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 999 1000 991 992 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1029 1030 1021 1022 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1062 1063 1054 1055 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1110 1111 1102 1103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1124 1125 1116 1117 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1142 1143 1134 1135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1156 1157 1148 1149 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1176 1177 1168 1169 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1198 1199 1190 1191 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1212 1213 1204 1205 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1230 1231 1222 1223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1244 1245 1236 1237 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1264 1265 1256 1257 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1283 1284 1275 1276 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 1321 1322 1313 1314 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1335 1336 1327 1328 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1336 1338 1328 1330 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CH</italic>
###xml 1338 1339 1330 1331 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</italic>
###xml 1338 1339 1330 1331 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>3</italic></sub>
###xml 1355 1356 1347 1348 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 1369 1370 1361 1362 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1370 1372 1362 1364 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CH</italic>
###xml 1372 1373 1364 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</italic>
###xml 1372 1373 1364 1365 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>3</italic></sub>
To a suspension of 42 mg 55% NaH (1.0 mmol) in 15 ml freshly distilled tetrahydrofuran (THF), 100 mg (0.44 mmol) of N,N-diethyl-2-(2-(4-hydroxyphenyl)-5,7-dimethylpyrazolo(1,5-alpha)pyrimidin-3-yl)acetamide (compound 1) [22] was added (Fig. 1). After the reaction mixture was refluxed for 30 min, a solution of 300 mg (0.87 mmol) ethyleneglycol ditosylate in 20 ml THF was quickly added to the hot reaction mixture. After another 18 h of refluxing, the reaction flask was cooled on ice and the reaction was quenched by slowly adding 50 ml of water. The mixture was extracted three times with 25 ml of dichloromethane. The combined organic layers were washed with 50 ml of water, dried on anhydrous sodium sulfate, and filtered. The product was purified by flash column chromatography (silica gel), using 3% methanol in dichloromethane as the eluent. The product was obtained as a light yellow solid in 59% yield (140 mg). 1H-NMR (CDCl3, 200 MHz): delta 7.83 (d, 2H, J = 8.1 Hz, tosyl), 7.74 (d, 2H, J = 8.8 Hz, Ar), 7.35 (d, 2H, J = 8.1 Hz, tosyl), 6.86 (d, 2H, J = 8.8 Hz, Ar), 6.52 (s, 1H, Ar), 4.39 (t, 2H, J = 4.6 Hz, CH2O), 4.19 (t, 2H, J = 4.6 Hz, CH2O), 3.95 (s, 2H, CH2C = O), 3.51 (q, 2H, J = 7.1 Hz, CH2N), 3.40 (q, 2H, J = 7.1 Hz, CH2N), 2.75 (s, 3H, CH3), 2.58 (s, 3H, CH3), 2.45 (s, 3H, tosyl), 1.21 (t, 3H, J = 7.1 Hz, CH2CH3), 1.11 (t, 3H, J = 7.1 Hz, CH2CH3).
###end p 23
###begin title 24
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N,N</italic>
###xml 72 77 72 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#945;</italic>
N,N-diethyl-2-(2-(4-[2-fluoro-1-ethoxy]phenyl)-5,7-dimethylpyrazolo(1,5-alpha)pyrimidin-3-yl)acetamide (Compound 4, DPA-714)
###end title 24
###begin p 25
###xml 191 192 191 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 231 232 231 232 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sup>
###xml 243 244 243 244 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 256 261 256 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#948;</italic>
###xml 275 276 271 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 305 306 301 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 354 355 350 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 366 367 362 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 381 382 377 378 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 400 401 396 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 412 413 408 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 427 428 423 424 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 447 448 443 444 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 467 468 463 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 481 482 477 478 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 499 500 495 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 513 514 509 510 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 533 534 529 530 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 552 553 548 549 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sub>
###xml 569 570 565 566 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 583 584 579 580 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 584 586 580 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CH</italic>
###xml 586 587 582 583 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</italic>
###xml 586 587 582 583 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>3</italic></sub>
###xml 603 604 599 600 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J</italic>
###xml 617 618 613 614 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 618 620 614 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CH</italic>
###xml 620 621 616 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</italic>
###xml 620 621 616 617 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>3</italic></sub>
Reference material of DPA-714 (compound 4) was prepared as described for compound 3, except 2-fluoroethyl tosylate was used as the alkylating agent instead of ethyleneglycol ditosylate (Fig. 1). Yield was 80% (light yellow solid). 1H-NMR (CDCl3, 200 MHz): delta 7.74 (d, 2H, J = 8.1 Hz, Ar), 6.99 (d, 2H, J = 8.1 Hz, Ar), 6.54 (s, 1H, Ar), 4.77 (dd, 2H, J = 2.9 Hz, J = 47.6 Hz, CH2F), 4.26 (dd, 2H, J = 2.9 Hz, J = 27.5 Hz, CH2O), 4.05 (s, 2H, CH2C=O), 3.51 (q, 2H, J = 7.0 Hz, CH2N), 3.41 (q, 2H, J = 7.0 Hz, CH2N), 2.78 (s, 3H, CH3), 2.64 (s, 3H, CH3), 1.23 (t, 3H, J = 7.0 Hz, CH2CH3), 1.12 (t, 3H, J = 7.0 Hz, CH2CH3).
###end p 25
###begin title 26
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 16 18 16 18 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
[18F]-DPA-714 ([18F]-Compound 4)
###end title 26
###begin p 27
###xml 1 3 1 3 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 177 179 177 179 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 338 340 332 334 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 531 532 519 520 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 534 535 522 523 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 621 623 609 611 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 749 750 736 737 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 752 753 739 740 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 1332 1333 1316 1317 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1335 1336 1319 1320 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 1466 1467 1448 1449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
[18F]Fluoride was eluted from a Waters QMA anion exchange cartridge with 5 mg potassium carbonate in 1 ml of water and collected into a vial containing 20 mg kryptofix[2.2.2]. [18F]KF/kryptofix[2.2.2] was dried by azeotropic distillation with acetonitrile at 130degreesC. A solution of 1 mg compound 3 in 0.5 ml dry DMF was added to the [18F]KF/kryptofix complex. The reaction mixture was allowed to react for 10 min at 100degreesC. After cooling, the reaction mixture was diluted with water and HPLC eluent (acetonitrile/0.1 M NaH2PO4 (45/55)) and passed through an Alumina N seppak to remove the majority of unreacted [18F]fluoride. The product was purified by HPLC using a SymmetryPrep C18 column (7 mum, 7.8 x 300 mm) with acetonitrile/0.1 M NaH2PO4 (45/55) as the eluent (flow 5 ml/min). To remove the organic solvents from the product, the collected HPLC fraction (retention time 11 min) was diluted with 15 ml of water and passed through an Oasis HLB 30 mg (1 cc) cartridge. The cartridge was washed with 5 ml of water and subsequently eluted with 0.7 ml of ethanol and 5 ml of water. The product was sterilized by filtration over a 22-mum Millex LG filter. The product was obtained in 17 +/- 8% radiochemical yield. Quality control was performed by HPLC, using a Novapak C18 column (150 x 3.9 mm) with acetonitrile/25 mM NaH2PO4 (35/65) as the eluent at a flow of 1 ml/min. The radiochemical purity was >99% and the specific activity was 80 +/- 35 MBq/nmol (n = 11).
###end p 27
###begin title 28
Animals
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 398 408 388 398 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ad libitum</italic>
###xml 576 578 566 568 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 582 583 572 573 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 594 595 584 585 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 603 605 593 595 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 617 618 607 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 629 631 619 621 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 643 644 633 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 703 705 693 695 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 709 710 699 700 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 721 722 711 712 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 730 732 720 722 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 744 745 734 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 756 758 746 748 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 770 771 760 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 888 890 878 880 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 894 895 884 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 906 907 896 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 915 917 905 907 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 929 930 919 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 941 943 931 933 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 955 956 945 946 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 35 39 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 121 125 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 429 433 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 487 491 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 540 544 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 651 655 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 670 675 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 677 680 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 782 786 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 801 806 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 837 840 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 987 991 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
Male outbred Wistar-Unilever (SPF) rats (weight 287 +/- 38 g) were obtained from Harlan (Lelystad, The Netherlands). The rats were individually housed in Macrolon cages (38 x 26 x 24 cm) on a layer of wood shavings in a room with constant temperature (21 +/- 2degreesC) and fixed, 12-h light-dark regime. Food (standard laboratory chow, RMH-B, Hope Farms, The Netherlands) and water were available ad libitum. After arrival, the rats were allowed to acclimatize for at least 7 days. The rats were randomly divided into nine groups: control rats (control) scanned with either [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (n = 5), [11C]-DPA-713 (n = 5), or [18F]-DPA-714 (n = 5), rats infected with HSV-1 (HSE) scanned with either [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (n = 9), [11C]-DPA-713 (n = 9), or [18F]-DPA-714 (n = 9), and rats infected with HSV-1 and pre-treated with PK11195 (HSE pre-treated with PK11195) scanned with either [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (n = 4), [11C]-DPA-713 (n = 4), or [18F]-DPA-714 (n = 4). After PET scanning, the rats were killed and the ex vivo biodistribution of the tracers was determined. The study was approved by the Animal Ethics Committee of the University of Groningen, The Netherlands.
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 0 5 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
HSV-1 Inoculation
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 330 331 329 330 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">7</sup>
###xml 4 9 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 141 145 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 248 253 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 411 415 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 513 517 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
The HSV-1 strain was obtained from a clinical isolate, cultured in Vero cells and assayed for plaque forming units (PFU) per milliliter. The rats were slightly anaesthetized with 5% isoflurane (Pharmachemie BV, The Netherlands) and inoculated with HSV-1 by the application of 100 mul of phosphate-buffered saline (PBS) with 1 x 107 PFU of virus on the nostrils (50 mul per nostril) with a micropipette. Control rats were treated similarly by the application of 100 mul PBS without virus. Clinical symptoms in all rats were scored daily after the inoculation by the same observer.
###end p 31
###begin title 32
Immunohistochemistry
###end title 32
###begin p 33
###xml 58 63 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 73 77 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 110 114 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 517 521 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 676 682 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">Rabbit</span>
###xml 856 860 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">Goat</span>
###xml 866 872 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">Rabbit</span>
###xml 946 950 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
Immunohistochemical staining was performed in control and HSV-1-infected rats on day 7 after inoculation. The rats were euthanized and the brains were removed and frozen at -80degreesC. Coronal brain sections of 10 mum were cut at -18degreesC using a cryostat (Leica Microsystems, Germany). Sections were collected on slides, vacuum-dried, fixated for 20 min in paraformaldehyde (4% in 100 nM PBS), and washed three times for 5 min in 100 nM PBS. To block non-specific binding, sections were incubated with 5% normal goat serum in PBS containing 3% triton and washed for 5 min in 100 nM PBS. Sections were incubated overnight at 4degreesC with the primary antibody (Anti Iba1 Rabbit (1:750), Wako Chemicals, USA). After incubation, sections were washed three times for 5 min in 100 nM PBS and incubated for 1 h with the secondary antibody (FITC-conjugated Goat Anti Rabbit IgG (1:250), Jackson ImmunoResearch Laboratories Inc., USA) in 1% normal goat serum in PBS containing 3% triton. As a negative control, sections were only incubated with the secondary antibody. Subsequently, sections were washed three times for 5 min in PBS and mounted with Mowiol mounting medium. The fluorescence was examined by using a microscope (Zeiss Axioskop 2, Carl Zeiss Microimaging Inc., Germany) in combination with the Leica Application Suite (Version 2.3.3 R1, Leica, Germany).
###end p 33
###begin title 34
PET Studies
###end title 34
###begin p 35
###xml 679 681 679 681 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 685 686 685 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 733 735 728 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 786 788 776 778 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 963 965 948 950 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 969 970 954 955 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 985 987 970 972 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 1030 1032 1015 1017 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 140 145 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 151 155 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 344 348 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
PET scans were performed when robust clinical signs of infection appeared, which was either on day 6 or on day 7 after the inoculation with HSV-1. The rats were anesthesized by an intraperitoneal injection of medetomidine (Domitor, Pfizer, The Netherlands, 0.2 mg/kg) and ketamine (Ketanest, Pfizer, The Netherlands, 25 mg/kg), after which the rats were positioned in the small animal PET camera (Focus 220, Siemens Medical Solutions USA, Inc.) in transaxial position with their heads in the field of view. A transmission scan of 515 s with a Co-57 point source was obtained for the correction of attenuation by tissue. After the transmission scan was completed, the PET tracer [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (65 +/- 22 MBq, 0.71 +/- 0.48 mug), [11C]-DPA-713 (82 +/- 23 MBq, 0.91 +/- 0.31 mug), or [18F]-DPA-714 (37 +/- 12 MBq, 0.36 +/- 0.18 mug) was injected via the penile vein. Simultaneous with the injection of the PET tracer, an emission scan of 62 min was started for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and a PET scan of 120 min for [18F]-DPA-714. In the pre-treated group, unlabeled PK11195 (Sigma-Aldrich, USA, 5 mg/kg in dimethylsulfoxide at a concentration of 10 mg/ml) was administered via the tail vein 5 min prior to injection of the PET tracer.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 134 136 134 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 140 141 140 141 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 156 158 156 158 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 194 196 194 196 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
The list-mode data of the emission scans was separated into 21 frames (8 x 30, 3 x 60, 2 x 120, 2 x 180, 3 x 300, and 3 x 600 s) for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and into 28 frames for [18F]-DPA-714 (8 x 30, 4 x 60, 3 x 120, 2 x 180, 4 x 300, and 8 x 600 s). Emission sinograms were iteratively reconstructed (OSEM2d, four iterations) after being normalized, corrected for attenuation, and corrected for decay of radioactivity.
###end p 36
###begin title 37
PET Image Analysis
###end title 37
###begin p 38
###xml 608 609 608 609 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sup>
###xml 787 789 787 789 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 793 794 793 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 809 811 809 811 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 830 831 830 831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">t</italic>
###xml 847 849 847 849 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
PET image analysis was performed using the Clinical Applications Packaging Program (CAPP5). Regions of interest were drawn around the bulbus olfactorius, frontal cortex, striatum, parietal/temporal/occipital cortex, brainstem, and cerebellum in a template PET scan that was co-registered with the PET scan of interest by image fusion. The time-activity curves per region of interest were determined in becquerel per cubic centimeter units and converted into standardized uptake values (SUV), defined as: [tissue activity concentration (MBq/g)]/[(injected dose (MBq)/body weight (g)]. It was assumed that 1 cm3 of brain tissue equals 1 g. To correct for the activity in plasma, each point on the time-activity curve (SUV) was divided by the ex vivo plasma uptake (SUV) at t = 60 min for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and at t = 120 min for [18F]-DPA-714 creating a tissue/plasma ratio.
###end p 38
###begin title 39
Ex Vivo Biodistribution
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 24 28 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
After the PET scan, the rats were killed by extirpation of the heart while under deep anesthesia. The brain was dissected into several brain areas, peripheral organs were excised, and blood was centrifuged to collect a plasma sample. The brain areas, peripheral organs, and plasma were weighed and analyzed for the amount of radioactivity by using a gammacounter (LKB Wallac, Turku, Finland). Tracer uptake is expressed as the SUV.
###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 183 187 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 272 275 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 276 280 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 371 374 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 375 379 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 449 452 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 453 457 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 468 471 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
To correct for activity of the tracers in plasma, the tissue/plasma ratio was calculated by dividing the uptake (SUV) in the different brain areas by the plasma uptake (SUV), for all rats individually. Subsequently, the TSPO-specific uptake was calculated for control and HSE rats. The specific uptake was calculated by subtracting the average tissue/plasma ratio of the HSE rats pre-treated with PK11195 from the tissue/plasma ratio of control and HSE rats, for each rat individually.
###end p 41
###begin title 42
Statistical Analysis
###end title 42
###begin p 43
###xml 189 191 187 189 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 195 196 193 194 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 208 210 206 208 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 227 229 225 227 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 781 783 779 781 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 787 788 785 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 800 802 798 800 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 819 821 817 819 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 1169 1171 1167 1169 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 1175 1176 1173 1174 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 1188 1190 1186 1188 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 1207 1209 1205 1207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 1226 1227 1224 1225 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3</sup>
###xml 1280 1282 1278 1280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">25</xref>
###xml 1353 1354 1351 1352 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">r</italic>
###xml 1391 1392 1389 1390 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 533 537 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 539 542 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 543 547 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 553 556 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 557 561 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1159 1163 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
All data are expressed as mean +/- standard deviation. Statistical analysis was performed using SPSS for Windows, version 14.0.2. Statistical analysis on differences between the uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714, which were obtained from the PET scan, was performed by one-way ANOVA. Per brain area, a Bonferonni post hoc test was used to determine if there were differences in uptake between the PET tracers. For the ex vivo biodistribution, statistical analysis on differences in uptake between control rats, HSE rats, and HSE rats pre-treated with PK11195 was performed by one-way ANOVA, using a Bonferonni post hoc test to compare the three conditions per brain area. Statistical analysis on differences between non-specific and specific uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714 was performed by one-way ANOVA, using a Bonferonni post hoc test to compare the uptake of the PET tracers per brain area. The time-activity curves were analyzed with the repeated measures general linear model of SPSS (version 14.0.2) using a Bonferroni post hoc test per brain area. Correlations of specific binding in control rats for [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714 with [3H]-PK11195 binding as determined by Kurumaji et al. [25] were assessed with Pearson's product moment correlation coefficient (r). Significance was reached when the p value was <0.05.
###end p 43
###begin title 44
Results
###end title 44
###begin title 45
Clinical Symptoms
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 534 536 534 536 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 540 541 540 541 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 556 558 556 558 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 653 655 653 655 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 730 732 728 730 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 736 737 734 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 767 769 763 765 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 803 805 797 799 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 409 412 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 413 417 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 465 470 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 575 579 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 634 638 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 882 886 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
Clinical symptoms were scored daily up to 7 days post-inoculation and categorized into the following clinical scores: (0), no symptoms; (1), ruffled fur and irritated mouth, nose, and eyes; (2), behavioral signs, like stress and lethargy, and hunched posture; (3), posterior paralysis and impairment of motor function; and (4), severe paralysis, labored breathing or death. The first clinical symptoms in the HSE rats were seen on day 4 or 5 after inoculation with HSV-1, after which the severity of the symptoms increased. For both [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, most rats had a score of 2 at the day of scanning, whereas most rats scanned with [18F]-DPA-714 had a score of 3. The average of the scores (2.44 +/- 0.73 for [11C]-(R)-PK11195, 2.11 +/- 0.78 for [11C]-DPA-713 and 2.67 +/- 0.71 for [18F]-DPA-714) did not differ significantly between groups. None of the control rats showed any clinical symptoms.
###end p 46

###xml 32 37 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 240 245 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 255 259 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 573 577 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 766 770 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 785 790 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 792 795 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 918 922 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1060 1064 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
At day 7 after inoculation with HSV-1, intense microglial activation was observed in the bulbus olfactorius, cerebellum, and brainstem (Fig. 2). In addition, mild microglial activation was also seen in the frontal cortex and hippocampus of HSV-1-infected rats. The activated microglia cells could be recognized by the rounded shape with short processes, showing that the microglia cells had converted to the macrophage-like state. Microglial activation in the brainstem was observed throughout the whole brainstem and could not be attributed to a specific area. In control rats, only ramified, resting microglia cells were observed in all brain areas. Fig. 2.Images (x400) of immunohistochemical staining of microglia cells with Iba, on day 7 after inoculation. For rats infected with HSV-1 (HSE) microglia are shown in the bulbus olfactorius, frontal cortex, hippocampus, cerebellum, and brainstem (a-e). For control rats, only the brainstem (f) is shown. The staining in this brain area is representative for the staining in all other brain areas of control rats.
###end p 48

###xml 300 303 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 304 308 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 334 338 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 438 442 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 696 699 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 700 704 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 729 733 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1083 1086 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1087 1091 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1116 1120 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1663 1667 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1686 1690 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1705 1710 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1712 1715 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1728 1732 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1747 1752 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1817 1820 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 3038 3041 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 3072 3075 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
The standardized uptake values obtained from the last 10 min of the PET scans are displayed in Table 1. The uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in the last 10 min of the scan was significantly higher in the bulbus olfactorius, frontal cortex, parietal/temporal/occipital cortex, cerebellum, and brainstem in HSE rats when compared to control rats. The uptake was consistent with the immunohistochemistry data. The [11C]-(R)-PK11195 uptake in the rats pre-treated with PK11195 was significantly decreased in the bulbus olfactorius, cerebellum, and brainstem. For [11C]-DPA-713, a significant increase in tracer uptake was found in the brainstem and a non-significant increase in the bulbus olfactorius of HSE rats, as compared to control rats. Also, [11C]-DPA-713 showed a statistically significant reduction in uptake by pre-treatment with PK11195 in the bulbus olfactorius, frontal cortex, parietal/temporal/occipital cortex, cerebellum and brainstem. The uptake of [18F]-DPA-714 derived from the PET scan was found to be non-significantly higher in the bulbus olfactorius and brainstem in HSE rats, as compared to control rats. No effective blocking of [18F]-DPA-714 by pre-treatment with PK11195 was found. The PET scan of [18F]-DPA-714 was 120 min, while the PET scan of both [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713 was 60 min. For comparison, the uptake [18F]-DPA-714 was also determined at 60 min, but no statistically significant differences were found between the uptake of [18F]-DPA-714 at 60 and 120 min. ###end p 51

The time&#8211;activity curves are expressed as tissue uptake divided by the ex vivo plasma uptake at <italic>t</italic>&#8201;=&#8201;60 for [<sup>11</sup>C]-(<italic>R</italic>)-PK11195 and [<sup>11</sup>C]-DPA-713, and at <italic>t</italic>&#8201;=&#8201;120 for [<sup>18</sup>F]-DPA-714. ###xml 762 765 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 766 770 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 817 821 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 838 842 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 927 930 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 931 935 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 981 985 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1004 1008 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1185 1189 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1253 1256 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1274 1278 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1585 1589 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1601 1605 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1620 1625 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1627 1630 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1637 1641 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1656 1661 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1723 1726 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 2062 2065 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
The time-activity curves of the brainstem are displayed in Fig. 3, to show the kinetics of the tracer over time. These time-activity curves were normalized for activity in plasma because tracer uptake in the brain is dependent on the tracer delivery from plasma. A change in plasma activity concentration due to, for example, pre-treatment with PK11195 can thus influence brain uptake. For plasma activity normalization, the uptake (SUV) on each individual time point was divided by the activity in plasma (SUV) as determined ex vivo on t = 60 for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and on t = 120 for [18F]-DPA-714. Post hoc analysis of the repeated measures general linear model revealed that the time-activity curve of [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in the brainstem of HSE rats was significantly higher than that of control rats (p < 0.005) and rats pre-treated with PK11195 (p < 0.005). For [11C]-DPA-713, the time-activity curve in HSE rats was significantly higher than in the control rats (p < 0.05) and in rats pre-treated with PK11195 (p < 0.005). In addition, the uptake of [11C]-DPA-713 over time was significantly reduced by pre-treatment with PK11195, even when compared to control rats (p < 0.05). No differences in time-activity curves of control, HSE, and pre-treated rats were found for [18F]-DPA-714 in the brainstem, although pre-treatment with PK11195 non-significantly reduced the uptake in the brainstem. Fig. 3.Time-activity curves (left) of the brainstem for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (a), [11C]-DPA-713 (b), and [18F]-DPA-714 (c), and small animal PET images (right) of control rats (control), rats infected with HSV-1 (HSE), and rats infected with HSV-1 injected with 5 mg/kg PK11195 5 min before tracer injection (HSE + PK11195). The time-activity curves are expressed as tissue uptake divided by the ex vivo plasma uptake at t = 60 for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and at t = 120 for [18F]-DPA-714. Statistically significant differences are indicated by *p < 0.05 and daggerp < 0.005. The small animal PET images display a coronal plane of the rat head at the level of the brainstem, in which the brain is delineated by a dashed line. The images are summed images between 16 and 60 min for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [11C]-DPA-713, and between 12 and 120 min for [18F]-DPA-714.
###end p 54

###xml 1230 1235 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1300 1303 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 2296 2299 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 2330 2333 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
An ex vivo biodistribution study of the three PET tracers was performed to confirm the results of the PET studies. In addition, biodistribution allows investigation of uptake in smaller brain areas than is possible with small animal PET imaging. The ex vivo biodistribution, expressed as mean SUV +/- SD, was consistent with the results obtained from the PET images. Uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (Table 2) in the bulbus olfactorius was increased in HSE rats as compared to control rats (1.59 vs. 1.20); however, this increase did not reach statistical significance. A significant increase of [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in HSE rats, as compared to control rats, was found in the medulla (1.29 vs. 0.61, p = 0.004), pons (1.54 vs. 0.59, p < 0.001), and cerebellum (0.88 vs. 0.51, p = 0.001). [11C]-(R)-PK11195 binding to the TSPO was blocked by administration of unlabeled PK11195, resulting in a significantly lower uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195 in the medulla, pons, cerebellum, and bulbus olfactorius. ###end p 57

###xml 132 136 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 205 209 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 379 382 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 383 387 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 438 442 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 630 634 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 801 805 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1038 1042 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1061 1065 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1080 1085 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1087 1090 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1104 1108 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1123 1128 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 1193 1196 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 2172 2175 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 2206 2209 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
The ex vivo biodistribution of [11C]-DPA-713 is shown in Table 3. As was found for [11C]-(R)-PK11195, the bulbus olfactorius in HSE rats showed an increase in [11C]-DPA-713 uptake when compared to control rats (1.30 vs. 0.93), but this difference did not reach statistical significance. Uptake in the medulla (1.09 vs. 0.46, p = 0.039) and the pons (1.12 vs. 0.46, p = 0.004) of HSE rats was significantly elevated as compared to control rats. This was confirmed by blocking studies. Unlabeled PK11195 significantly reduced [11C]-DPA-713 uptake in the bulbus olfactorius, pons, and medulla. The uptake of [11C]-DPA-713 in control rats was on average 26% lower (p < 0.005) than the uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, suggesting less non-specific binding. In addition, the brain uptake in PK11195 pre-treated rats was significantly lower for [11C]-DPA-713 than for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (p < 0.005). *p < 0.05 as compared to control, **p < 0.005 as compared to control, ***p < 0.05 as compared to HSE, ****p < 0.005 as compared to HSE
###end p 62

###xml 42 46 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 206 209 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 210 214 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 268 272 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 620 624 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 643 647 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 662 667 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 669 672 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 686 690 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 705 710 <span type="species:ncbi:10298?0.9377676277476449">HSV-1</span>
###xml 775 778 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1755 1758 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1789 1792 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
[18F]-DPA-714 uptake (Table 4) in control rats was significantly lower than [11C]-(R)-PK11195 uptake (on average 41%, p < 0.005). Significantly increased uptake of [18F]-DPA-714 was found in the medulla of HSE rats (0.40 vs. 0.81, p = 0.004), when compared to control rats, while a non-significant increase in uptake was found in the bulbus olfactorius (0.55 vs. 0.88). No effective blocking of [18F]-DPA-714 uptake was found after administration of unlabeled PK11195. ###end p 63

###begin p 65
###xml 1 2 1 2 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 36 37 36 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 73 74 73 74 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>

###begin p 66
###xml 70 72 70 72 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 76 77 76 77 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 89 91 89 91 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 108 110 108 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
###xml 210 212 210 212 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 216 217 216 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 351 353 351 353 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">11</sup>
###xml 369 371 369 371 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">18</sup>
Ex vivo biodistribution in peripheral organs showed a high uptake of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714 in TSPO expressing organs, like the lungs and adrenals. In both the lungs and adrenals, [11C]-(R)-PK11195 uptake was effectively blocked by unlabeled PK11195, resulting in a significant reduction in uptake, whereas the uptake of [11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714 was only significantly blocked in the lungs, but not in the adrenals.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
Ex Vivo Biodistribution: Specific Binding
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 59 62 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 63 67 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 487 490 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
The ex vivo biodistribution showed an increased binding in HSE rats as compared to controls and a decreased binding after pre-treatment with PK11195, for all three PET tracers. However, plasma levels of the tracer were also found to be different between the three PET tracers and between treatment groups. Since tracer accumulation in the brain is dependent on tracer delivery (and thus tracer concentration) from plasma, the brain uptake was corrected for plasma radioactivity for each rat individually to calculate the tissue/plasma ratios.
###end p 68

###xml 186 190 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 264 267 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 268 272 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 328 331 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 332 336 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 406 409 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 410 414 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 425 428 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
###xml 520 524 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 622 625 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 626 630 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 888 892 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1183 1187 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1332 1335 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1336 1340 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 1613 1616 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 1617 1621 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 3804 3807 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 3808 3812 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 3891 3894 <span type="species:ncbi:10298">HSE</span>
###xml 3903 3907 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
Non-specific binding and specific binding of [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714 are displayed in Table 5. Non-specific binding was defined as the tissue/plasma ratio of rats pre-treated with PK11195. Specific binding was calculated in control and HSE rats, by subtracting the average tissue/plasma ratio of the HSE rats pre-treated with PK11195 from the tissue/plasma ratio of control and HSE rats, for each rat individually. The rationale behind the definition of specific uptake is that the uptake in rats pre-treated with PK11195 represents non-specific binding only, whereas the uptake in control and HSE rats is due to both specific and non-specific binding. Non-specific binding was found to be statistically significantly lower in almost all brain areas for both [11C]-DPA-713 and [18F]-DPA-714, when compared to [11C]-(R)-PK11195. The specific binding in control rats was found to be significantly higher for [11C]-DPA-713 in the amygdala/piriform cortex, bulbus olfactorius, cerebellum, entorhinal cortex, medulla, parietal/temporal/occipital cortex, pons, and striatum, when compared to [11C]-(R)-PK11195. For [18F]-DPA-714, the specific uptake in control rats was significantly higher than [11C]-(R)-PK11195 uptake in the cingulate/frontopolar cortex, pons, and striatum. In addition, specific uptake in HSE rats was found to be significantly higher for [11C]-DPA-713 in the amygdala/piriform cortex, bulbus olfactorius, entorhinal cortex, hippocampus, medulla, and parietal/temporal/occipital cortex as compared to [11C]-(R)-PK11195. No significant differences in specific binding in HSE rats were found between [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and [18F]-DPA-714. ###xml 32 36 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
###xml 979 983 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rats</span>
The specific binding in control rats showed a good correlation with [3H]-PK11195 binding (Fig. 4) as was measured by Kurumaji et al. [25] for all three PET tracers. The best correlation was found for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 that had a R of 0.96 (p = 0.0006), followed by [11C]-DPA-713 with a R of 0.87 (p = 0.01) and [18F]-DPA-714 with a R of 0.77 (p = 0.04). Although the best correlation was found for [11C]-(R)-PK11195, the slope of the linear regression was highest for [11C]-DPA-713 (0.016; compared to 0.010 for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 and 0.005 for [18F]-DPA-714), which indicates that [11C]-DPA-713 uptake might be most sensitive to changes in TSPO expression. Although these results seem to depend on the bulbus olfactorius, which has the highest uptake, the correlation remained good after removal of this data point from the regression analysis. In addition, the slope of the linear regression remained highest for [11C]-DPA-713. Fig. 4.Correlation of specific binding in control rats for [11C]-(R)-PK11195, [11C]-DPA-713, and [18F]-DPA-714 with [3H]-PK11195 binding as determined by Kurumaji et al. [25]. The R was 0.96 for [11C]-(R)-PK11195 (p = 0.0006; y = 0.36 + 0.010x), 0.87 for [11C]-DPA-713 (p = 0.0116; y = 1.79 + 0.016x), and 0.77 for [18F]-DPA-714 (p = 0.0427; y = 1.35 + 0.005x).
###end p 73

###xml 263 264 263 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">p</italic>
###xml 275 276 275 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">y</italic>
###xml 291 292 291 292 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">x</italic>
